## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models acceleration in a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where dv/dt depends on velocity v and time t. The absence of position x suggests either velocity-dependent forces (nonlinear damping), explicit time-dependent driving, or that position has been eliminated through a substitution.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (simple velocity-proportional force)
- Cubic nonlinearity in v: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity dependence)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (nonlinear damping with harmonic drive)
- Harmonic driving: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v (driven damped oscillator)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 (velocity-squared drag term)
- Polynomial velocity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 + c2 * v**3 (general polynomial nonlinearity in v)
- Driven with nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * v**2) * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (Van der Pol with drive)
- Sinusoidal restoring via time: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) + c3 * v (position replaced by time-phase relation)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping with forcing)
- Mathieu-type parametric: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * v (parametric excitation)
- Combined nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * v * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v**3 (multiplicative coupling with nonlinearity)
- Velocity-time product: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * t * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (time-varying damping coefficient)
- General driven nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 + c4 (most general driven nonlinear form)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Nonlinear damping in oscillators → odd-power velocity terms like v³, v⁵ that preserve time-reversal symmetry breaking
- Periodic driving forces → sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) additive terms representing external harmonic excitation
- Parametric excitation → multiplicative coupling of trigonometric time functions with velocity: cos(c*t)*v
- Self-excited oscillation (Van der Pol) → terms of form (1 - c*v²)*v producing limit cycles
- Absence of explicit position variable → position-dependent restoring force may appear as sinusoidal function of time if motion is quasi-periodic
- Energy-dependent damping → velocity terms with even-power coefficients like v²*sign(v) or v*|v| controlling amplitude
- Phase-space structure → acceleration as polynomial in v reflects the topology of phase portraits (limit cycles, separatrices)
- Frequency mixing in driven systems → products of trigonometric time terms at different frequencies indicate nonlinear resonance
